<li id="cite_note-added_fructose-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink noprint">↑ <sup><a href="#cite_ref-added_fructose_65-0">a</a> et <a href="#cite_ref-added_fructose_65-1">b</a></sup> </span><span class="reference-text"><span class="ouvrage" id="Di_NicolantonioO'KeefeLucan2015"><span class="ouvrage" id="James_J._Di_NicolantonioJames_H._O'KeefeC._Lucan2015"><abbr class="abbr indicateur-langue" title="Langue : anglais">(en)</abbr> James J. Di Nicolantonio, James H. O'Keefe et C. Lucan, <span lang="en">« <cite style="font-style:normal;">Added Fructose: a principal driver of type 2 diabetes mellitus and its consequences</cite> »</span>, <i><span class="lang-en" lang="en">Mayo Clinic Proceedings</span></i>, <abbr class="abbr" title="volume">vol.</abbr> 90, <abbr class="abbr" title="numéro">n<sup>o</sup></abbr> 3,‎ <time class="nowrap" data-sort-value="2015-03" datetime="2015-03">mars 2015</time> <small style="line-height:1em;">(<a href="/wiki/Digital_Object_Identifier" title="Digital Object Identifier">DOI</a> <span class="plainlinks noarchive nowrap"><a class="external text" href="https://dx.doi.org/10.1016/j.mayocp.2014.12.019" rel="nofollow">10.1016/j.mayocp.2014.12.019</a></span>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.mayoclinicproceedings.org/article/S0025-6196%2815%2900040-3/abstract" rel="nofollow">lire en ligne</a>)</small><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Added+Fructose%3A+a+principal+driver+of+type+2+diabetes+mellitus+and+its+consequences&amp;rft.jtitle=Mayo+Clinic+Proceedings&amp;rft.issue=3&amp;rft.aulast=Di+Nicolantonio&amp;rft.aufirst=James+J.&amp;rft.au=James+H.+O%27Keefe&amp;rft.au=C.+Lucan&amp;rft.date=2015-03&amp;rft.volume=90&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1016%2Fj.mayocp.2014.12.019&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Ffr.wikipedia.org%3ASucre"></span></span></span> :<blockquote><p>« <span class="lang-en" lang="en">The existing basic science evidence, observational data, and clinic trial findings suggest that reducing consumption of added sugars, particularly added fructose, could translate to reduced diabetes-related morbidity and potentially premature mortality. […] At current levels, sugar consumption and fructose consumption in particular—in concentrations and contexts not seen in natural whole foods—are fueling a worsening epidemic of type 2 diabetes. Even without existing data for the duration of diabetes’ 20-year incubation period, shorter-term basic science evidence, observational data, and clinical trial findings present compelling evidence to suggest that added sugar and especially added fructose (provided from HFCS and sucrose) present a serious and increasing public health problem.</span> »</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-anand2015-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink noprint">↑ <sup><a href="#cite_ref-anand2015_66-0">a</a> <a href="#cite_ref-anand2015_66-1">b</a> <a href="#cite_ref-anand2015_66-2">c</a> <a href="#cite_ref-anand2015_66-3">d</a> <a href="#cite_ref-anand2015_66-4">e</a> et <a href="#cite_ref-anand2015_66-5">f</a></sup> </span><span class="reference-text"><span class="ouvrage" id="AnandHawkesde_Souza2015"><span class="ouvrage" id="S.S._AnandC._HawkesR.J._de_Souza2015"><abbr class="abbr indicateur-langue" title="Langue : anglais">(en)</abbr> S.S. <span class="nom_auteur">Anand</span>, C. <span class="nom_auteur">Hawkes</span>, R.J. <span class="nom_auteur">de Souza</span> <i><abbr class="abbr" title="et alii (et d’autres)">et al.</abbr></i>, <span lang="en">« <cite style="font-style:normal;">Food Consumption and its Impact on Cardiovascular Disease: Importance of Solutions Focused on the Globalized Food SystemA Report From the Workshop Convened by the World Heart Federation</cite> »</span>, <i><span class="lang-en" lang="en">Journal of the American College of Cardiology</span></i>, <abbr class="abbr" title="volume">vol.</abbr> 66, <abbr class="abbr" title="numéro">n<sup>o</sup></abbr> 14,‎ <time class="nowrap" data-sort-value="2015-10-06" datetime="2015-10-06">6 octobre 2015</time>, <abbr class="abbr" title="pages">p.</abbr> 1590–1614 <small style="line-height:1em;">(<a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Serial_Number" title="International Standard Serial Number">ISSN</a> <span class="plainlinks noarchive"><a class="external text" href="https://www.worldcat.org/issn/0735-1097&amp;lang=fr" rel="nofollow">0735-1097</a></span>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S0735109715046215" rel="nofollow">résumé</a>)</small><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=Food+Consumption+and+its+Impact+on+Cardiovascular+Disease%3A+Importance+of+Solutions+Focused+on+the+Globalized+Food+SystemA+Report+From+the+Workshop+Convened+by+the+World+Heart+Federation&amp;rft.jtitle=Journal+of+the+American+College+of+Cardiology&amp;rft.issue=14&amp;rft.aulast=Anand&amp;rft.aufirst=S.S.&amp;rft.au=Hawkes%2C+C.&amp;rft.au=de+Souza%2C+R.J.&amp;rft.date=2015-10-06&amp;rft.volume=66&amp;rft.pages=1590%E2%80%931614&amp;rft.issn=0735-1097&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Ffr.wikipedia.org%3ASucre"></span></span></span> :<blockquote><p>« <span class="lang-en" lang="en">Robust data from systematic reviews and high-quality randomized controlled trials (RCTs) support a harmful effect of highly refined, high–glycemic load (GL) carbohydrates. A meta-analysis of observational studies indicated that high–glycemic index (GI) foods are associated with T2DM.[…]T2DM risk in individuals with the highest GL and lowest cereal fiber is 2.5-fold that of those with the lowest GL and highest cereal fiber diet. […] A meta-analysis of 310,819 participants and 15,043 cases of T2DM reported a 26% increased T2DM risk among those consuming 1 to 2 SSB servings/day compared with nonconsumers.</span> »</p></blockquote></span>

title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.atitle=It+is+time+to+bust+the+myth+of+physical+inactivity+and+obesity%3A+you+cannot+outrun+a+bad+diet&amp;rft.jtitle=British+Journal+of+Sports+Medicine&amp;rft.aulast=Malhotra&amp;rft.aufirst=A.&amp;rft.au=Noakes%2C+T.&amp;rft.au=Phinney%2C+S.&amp;rft.date=2015-04-22&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.1136%2Fbjsports-2015-094911&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F25904145&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbjsm.bmj.com%2Fcontent%2Fearly%2F2015%2F04%2F21%2Fbjsports-2015-094911&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Ffr.wikipedia.org%3ASucre"></span></span></span> :<blockquote><p>« <span class="lang-en" lang="en">Coca Cola, who spent $3.3 billion on advertising in 2013, pushes a message that ‘all calories count’; they associate their products with sport, suggesting it is ok to consume their drinks as long as you exercise. However science tells us this is misleading and wrong. It is where the calories come from that is crucial. Sugar calories promote fat storage and hunger. Fat calories induce fullness or ‘satiation’. causation. A recently published critical review in nutrition concluded that dietary carbohydrate restriction is the single most effective intervention for reducing all the features of the metabolic syndrome and should be the first approach in diabetes management, with benefits occurring even without weight loss.</span> »</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
